</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"><a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect">Franklin Delano Roosevelt</a>'s January&#160;6, 1941 <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Union_Address" title="State of the Union Address" class="mw-redirect">State of the Union Address</a> introducing the theme of the <a href="/wiki/Four_Freedoms" title="Four Freedoms">Four Freedoms</a> (starting at 32:02)</div>
</div>
<hr /></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Roosevelt's third term was dominated by World War II. Roosevelt slowly began re-armament in 1938, although he was facing strong isolationist sentiment from leaders like Senators <a href="/wiki/William_Borah" title="William Borah">William Borah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Taft" title="Robert A. Taft">Robert A. Taft</a>. By 1940, re-armament was in high gear, with bipartisan support, partly to expand and re-equip the Army and Navy and partly to become the "Arsenal of Democracy" supporting Britain, France, China and (after June&#160;1941), the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> As Roosevelt took a firmer stance against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers" class="mw-redirect">Axis Powers</a>, American isolationists (including <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lindbergh" title="Charles Lindbergh">Charles Lindbergh</a> and <a href="/wiki/America_First_Committee" title="America First Committee">America First</a>) vehemently attacked the President as an irresponsible warmonger.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Roosevelt initiated <a href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI" class="mw-redirect">FBI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> investigations of his loudest critics, though no legal actions resulted.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> Unfazed by these criticisms and confident in the wisdom of his foreign policy initiatives, FDR continued his twin policies of preparedness and aid to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> coalition. On December&#160;29, 1940, he delivered his Arsenal of Democracy fireside chat, in which he made the case for involvement in the war directly to the American people. A week later he delivered his famous <a href="/wiki/Four_Freedoms" title="Four Freedoms">Four Freedoms</a> speech laying out the case for an American defense of basic rights throughout the world.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/220px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/330px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/440px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="587" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roosevelt and <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> aboard <i>HMS Prince of Wales</i> for 1941 Atlantic Charter meeting.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The homefront was subject to dynamic social changes throughout the war, though domestic issues were no longer Roosevelt's most urgent policy concern. The military buildup spurred economic growth. Unemployment fell in half from 7.7 million in spring 1940 (when the first accurate statistics were compiled) to 3.4 million in fall 1941 and fell in half again to 1.5 million in fall 1942, out of a labor force of 54 million.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>c<span>]</span></a></sup> There was a growing labor shortage, accelerating the second wave of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a> of African Americans, farmers and rural populations to manufacturing centers. African Americans from the South went to California and other West Coast states for new jobs in the defense industry. To pay for increased government spending, in 1941 FDR proposed that Congress enact an income tax rate of 99.5% on all income over $100,000; when the proposal failed, he issued an executive order imposing an income tax of 100% on income over $25,000, which Congress rescinded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchweikartAllen2004602_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchweikartAllen2004602-227"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invaded</a> the Soviet Union in June&#160;1941, Roosevelt agreed to extend Lend-Lease to the Soviets. Thus, Roosevelt had committed the U.S. to the Allied side with a policy of "all aid short of war."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChurchill1977119_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChurchill1977119-228"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> Execution of the aid fell victim to foot dragging in the administration so FDR appointed a special assistant, Wayne Coy, to expedite matters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970115_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970115-229"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year a German submarine fired on the U.S. destroyer <i>Greer,</i> and Roosevelt declared that the U.S. Navy would assume an escort role for Allied convoys in the Atlantic as far east as Great Britain and would fire upon German ships or submarines (<a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boats</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Kriegsmarine" title="Kriegsmarine">Kriegsmarine</a> if they entered the U.S. Navy zone. This "shoot on sight" policy effectively declared Naval war on Germany and was favored by Americans by a margin of 2-to-1.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970141.E2.80.9342_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970141.E2.80.9342-230"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Roosevelt and Churchill conducted a highly secret bilateral meeting in Argentia, Newfoundland, and on August&#160;14, 1941, drafted the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>, conceptually outlining global wartime and postwar goals. All the Allies endorsed it. This was the first of several <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_War_II_conferences" title="List of World War II conferences">wartime conferences</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970126.E2.80.9328_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970126.E2.80.9328-231"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> Churchill and Roosevelt would meet ten more times in person.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther195015.E2.80.9316_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther195015.E2.80.9316-232"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> In July&#160;1941, Roosevelt had ordered <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War" title="United States Secretary of War">Secretary of War</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Stimson" title="Henry Stimson" class="mw-redirect">Henry Stimson</a>, to begin planning for total American military involvement. The resulting "Victory Program" provided the Army's estimates necessary for the total mobilization of manpower, industry, and logistics to defeat Germany and Japan. The program also planned to dramatically increase aid to the Allied nations and to have ten million men in arms, half of whom would be ready for deployment abroad in 1943. Roosevelt was firmly committed to the Allied cause and these plans had been formulated before Japan's <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Attack on Pearl Harbor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChurchill1977119_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChurchill1977119-228"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Congress was debating a modification of the Neutrality Act in October&#160;1941, when the <a href="/wiki/USS_Kearny_(DD-432)" title="USS Kearny (DD-432)">USS <i>Kearny</i></a>, along with other ships, engaged a number of U-boats south of Iceland; the <i>Kearny</i> took fire and lost eleven crewmen. As a result, the amendment of the Neutrality Act to permit the arming of the merchant marine passed both houses, though by a slim margin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970148_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970148-233"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1942, war production increased dramatically, but fell short of the goals established by the President, due in part to manpower shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970333_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970333-234"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> The effort was also hindered by numerous strikes by union workers, especially in the coal mining and railroad industries, which lasted well into 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970343_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970343-235"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> The White House became the ultimate site for labor mediation, conciliation or arbitration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970338_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970338-237"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> One particular battle royal occurred, between Vice-President Wallace, who headed the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Economic_Warfare" title="Board of Economic Warfare">Board of Economic Warfare</a>, and Jesse Jones, in charge of the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Finance_Corporation" title="Reconstruction Finance Corporation">Reconstruction Finance Corporation</a>; both agencies assumed responsibility for acquisition of rubber supplies and came to loggerheads over funding. FDR resolved the dispute by dissolving both agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970341.E2.80.9342_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970341.E2.80.9342-238"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1944, the President requested that Congress enact legislation which would tax all unreasonable profits, both corporate and individual, and thereby support his declared need for over $10 billion in revenue for the war and other government measures. The Congress passed a revenue bill raising $2 billion, which FDR vetoed, though Congress in turn overrode him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970436_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970436-239"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pearl_Harbor_and_declarations_of_war">Pearl Harbor and declarations of war</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Events_leading_to_the_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Events leading to the attack on Pearl Harbor">Events leading to the attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Attack on Pearl Harbor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe_first" title="Europe first">Europe first</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:328px;max-width:328px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg/160px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg" width="160" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg/240px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg/320px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Japan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2173" data-file-height="2731" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg/160px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg" width="160" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg/240px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg/320px-Franklin_Roosevelt_signing_declaration_of_war_against_Germany.jpg 2x" data-file-width="923" data-file-height="1162" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Roosevelt signing declaration of war <a href="/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_upon_Japan" title="United States declaration of war upon Japan">against Japan</a> (left) on December&#160;8 and <a href="/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_upon_Germany_(1941)" title="United States declaration of war upon Germany (1941)">against Germany</a> (right) on December&#160;11, 1941.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When Japan occupied northern <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a> in late 1940, FDR authorized increased aid to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)" class="mw-redirect">Republic of China</a>, a policy that won widespread popular support. In July&#160;1941, after Japan occupied the remainder of Indo-China, he cut off the sale of oil to Japan, which thus lost more than 95 percent of its oil supply. Roosevelt continued negotiations with the Japanese government, primarily through Secretary Hull. <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Japan" title="Prime Minister of Japan">Japan Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Fumimaro_Konoe" title="Fumimaro Konoe">Fumimaro Konoye</a> desired a summit conference with FDR which the US rejected. Konoye was replaced with <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_War_of_Japan" title="Ministry of War of Japan">Minister of War</a> <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Tojo" title="Hideki Tojo">Hideki Tojo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970134.E2.80.9346_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970134.E2.80.9346-240"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, Roosevelt started sending long-range B-17 bombers to the Philippines.</p>
<p>FDR felt that an attack by the Japanese was probable&#160;– most likely in the Dutch East Indies or Thailand.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970159_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970159-241"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> On December&#160;4, 1941, <i>The Chicago Tribune</i> published the complete text of "<a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Five" title="Rainbow Five" class="mw-redirect">Rainbow Five</a>", a top-secret war plan drawn up by the War Department. It dealt chiefly with mobilization issues, calling for a 10-million-man army.</p>
<p>The great majority of scholars have rejected the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theory" title="Pearl Harbor advance-knowledge conspiracy theory">conspiracy thesis</a> that Roosevelt, or any other high government officials, knew in advance about the Japanese attack on Pearl Harbor. The Japanese had kept their secrets closely guarded. Senior American officials were aware that war was imminent, but they did not expect an attack on Pearl Harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007523.E2.80.9339_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007523.E2.80.9339-242"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On the morning of December&#160;7, 1941, the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">struck the U.S. naval base at Pearl Harbor with a surprise attack</a>, knocking out the main American battleship fleet and killing 2,403 American servicemen and civilians. Roosevelt called for war in his famous "<a href="/wiki/Infamy_Speech" title="Infamy Speech">Infamy Speech</a>" to Congress, in which he said: "Yesterday, December&#160;7, 1941&#160;— a date which will live in infamy&#160;— the United States of America was suddenly and deliberately attacked by naval and air forces of the Empire of Japan."</p>
<p>In 1942 Roosevelt set up a new military command structure with Admiral <a href="/wiki/Ernest_J._King" title="Ernest J. King" class="mw-redirect">Ernest J. King</a> as Chief of Naval Operations in complete control of the Navy and Marines; General <a href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall" title="George C. Marshall" class="mw-redirect">George C. Marshall</a> in charge of the Army and in nominal control of the Air Force, which in practice was commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Hap_Arnold" title="Hap Arnold" class="mw-redirect">Hap Arnold</a>. Roosevelt formed a new body, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>, which made the final decisions on American military strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> The Joint Chiefs was a White House agency and was chaired by Admiral <a href="/wiki/William_D._Leahy" title="William D. Leahy">William D. Leahy</a>. When dealing with Europe, the Joint Chiefs met with their British counterparts and formed the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Combined Chiefs of Staff">Combined Chiefs of Staff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Unlike the political leaders of the other major powers, Roosevelt rarely overrode his military advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarrabee1987_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarrabee1987-245"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> His civilian appointees handled the draft and procurement of men and equipment, but no civilians&#160;– not even the secretaries of War or Navy, had a voice in strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>d<span>]</span></a></sup> Roosevelt avoided the State Department and conducted high level diplomacy through his aides, especially <a href="/wiki/Harry_Hopkins" title="Harry Hopkins">Harry Hopkins</a>. Since Hopkins also controlled $50 billion in <a href="/wiki/Lend_Lease" title="Lend Lease" class="mw-redirect">Lend Lease</a> funds given to the Allies, they paid attention to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherwood1949_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherwood1949-247"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_plans">War plans</span></h3>
<p>After Pearl Harbor, antiwar sentiment in the United States evaporated overnight. On December&#160;11, 1941, Germany and Italy declared war on the United States, which responded in kind.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESainsbury1994184_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESainsbury1994184-248"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> Roosevelt and his military advisers implemented a war strategy with the objectives of halting the German advances in the Soviet Union and in North Africa; launching an invasion of western Europe with the aim of crushing Nazi Germany between two fronts; and saving China and defeating Japan. Public opinion, however, gave priority to the destruction of Japan, so American forces were sent chiefly to the Pacific in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the opening weeks of the war, Japan had conquered the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Philippines</a>, and the British and Dutch colonies in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, capturing <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> in February&#160;1942. Furthermore, Japan cut off the overland supply route to China.</p>
<p>Roosevelt met with Churchill in late December and planned a broad informal alliance among the U.S., Britain, China and the Soviet Union. This included Churchill's initial plan to invade North Africa (called <a href="/wiki/Operation_Gymnast" title="Operation Gymnast" class="mw-redirect">Operation Gymnast</a>) and the primary plan of the U.S. generals for a western Europe invasion, focused directly on Germany (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Sledgehammer" title="Operation Sledgehammer">Operation Sledgehammer</a>). An agreement was also reached for a centralized command and offensive in the Pacific theater called <a href="/wiki/ABDA" title="ABDA" class="mw-redirect">ABDA</a> (American, British, Dutch, Australian) to save China and defeat Japan. Nevertheless, the Atlantic First strategy was intact, to Churchill's great satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970180.E2.80.9385_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970180.E2.80.9385-250"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> On New Year's Day 1942, Churchill and FDR issued the "Declaration by United Nations", representing 26 countries in opposition to the Tripartite Pact of Germany, Italy and Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970185_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970185-251"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internment_of_Germans.2C_Japanese_and_Italians">Internment of Germans, Japanese and Italians</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_American_internment" title="German American internment" class="mw-redirect">German American internment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American_internment" title="Japanese American internment" class="mw-redirect">Japanese American internment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_American_internment" title="Italian American internment" class="mw-redirect">Italian American internment</a></div>
<p>When the war began, the danger of a Japanese attack on the coast led to growing pressure to move people of Japanese descent away from the coastal region. This pressure grew due to fears of terrorism, espionage, and/or sabotage; it was also related to anti-Japanese competition and discrimination. On February&#160;19, 1942, President Roosevelt signed <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_9066" title="Executive Order 9066">Executive Order 9066</a>, which relocated hundreds of thousands of the "Issei" (first generation of Japanese immigrants who did not have U.S. citizenship) and their children, "Nisei" (who had dual citizenship). They were forced to give up their properties and businesses, and transported to hastily built camps in interior, harsh locations.</p>
<p>After both Nazi Germany and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)" class="mw-redirect">Fascist Italy</a> declared war on the United States in December&#160;1941, many <a href="/wiki/German-American_internment" title="German-American internment" class="mw-redirect">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian-American_internment" title="Italian-American internment" class="mw-redirect">Italian</a> citizens who had not taken out American citizenship were arrested or interned.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_strategy">War strategy</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Casablanca-Conference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/220px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg" width="220" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/330px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/440px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="578" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Roosevelt and Churchill at the <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Conference" title="Casablanca Conference">Casablanca Conference</a> (January&#160;1943)</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cairo_conference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/220px-Cairo_conference.jpg" width="220" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/330px-Cairo_conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/440px-Cairo_conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="442" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, Roosevelt, and Winston Churchill at the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Conference" title="Cairo Conference">Cairo Conference</a> (December&#160;1943)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "Big Three" (Roosevelt, Churchill, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>), together with Generalissimo <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, cooperated informally on a plan in which American and British troops concentrated in the West; Soviet troops fought on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern front</a>; and Chinese, British and American troops fought in Asia and the Pacific. The Allies formulated strategy in a series of high-profile conferences as well as contact through diplomatic and military channels. Roosevelt guaranteed that the U.S. would be the "Arsenal of Democracy" by shipping $50&#160;billion of <a href="/wiki/Lend_Lease" title="Lend Lease" class="mw-redirect">Lend Lease</a> supplies, primarily to Britain and to the USSR, China and other Allies.</p>
<p>In October&#160;1942, the President was advised that military resources were desperately needed at Guadalcanal to prevent overrunning by the Japanese. FDR heeded the advice, redirected armaments and the Japanese Pacific offensive was stalled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970284_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970284-253"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Allies undertook the invasions of French <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Operation Torch</a>) in November&#160;1942. FDR very much desired the assault be initiated before election day, but did not order it. FDR and Churchill had another war <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Conference" title="Casablanca Conference">conference in Casablanca</a> in January&#160;1943; Stalin declined an invitation. The Allies agreed strategically that the Mediterranean focus be continued, with the cross-channel invasion coming later, followed by concentration of efforts in the Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970318.E2.80.9324_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970318.E2.80.9324-254"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> Roosevelt also championed General <a href="/wiki/Henri_Giraud" title="Henri Giraud">Henri Giraud</a> as leader of <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free France</a> against General <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> Hitler reinforced his military in North Africa, with the result that the Allied efforts there suffered a temporary setback; Allied attempts to counterbalance this were successful, but resulted in war supplies to the USSR being delayed, as well as the second war front.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970327.E2.80.9328_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970327.E2.80.9328-256"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, their assault pursued into <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Husky" title="Operation Husky" class="mw-redirect">Operation Husky</a>) followed in July&#160;1943, and of Italy (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Avalanche" title="Operation Avalanche" class="mw-redirect">Operation Avalanche</a>) in September&#160;1943. In 1943, it was apparent to FDR that Stalin, while bearing the brunt of Germany's offensive, had not had sufficient opportunity to participate in war conferences. The President made a concerted effort to arrange a one-on-one meeting with Stalin, in Fairbanks. However, when Stalin learned that Roosevelt and Churchill had postponed the cross-channel invasion a second time, he cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970371_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970371-257"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">strategic bombing campaign</a> was escalated in 1944, pulverizing all major German cities and cutting off oil supplies. It was a 50–50 British-American operation. Roosevelt picked <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>, and not <a href="/wiki/George_Marshall" title="George Marshall">George Marshall</a>, to head the Allied cross-channel invasion, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation Overlord</a> that began on <a href="/wiki/D-Day" title="D-Day" class="mw-redirect">D-Day</a>, June&#160;6, 1944. Some of the most costly battles of the war ensued after the invasion, and the Allies were blocked on the German border in the "<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a>" in December&#160;1944. When Roosevelt died on April&#160;12, 1945, Allied forces were closing in on Berlin.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, in the Pacific, the Japanese advance reached its maximum extent by June&#160;1942, when the U.S. Navy scored a decisive victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>. American and Australian forces then began a slow and costly progress called <a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)" title="Leapfrogging (strategy)">island hopping</a> or <a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging" title="Leapfrogging">leapfrogging</a> through the Pacific Islands, with the objective of gaining bases from which strategic airpower could be brought to bear on Japan and from which Japan could ultimately be invaded. In contrast to Hitler, Roosevelt took no direct part in the tactical naval operations, though he approved strategic decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970228_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970228-258"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> FDR gave way in part to insistent demands from the public and Congress that more effort be devoted against Japan; he always insisted on Germany first.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_planning">Post-war planning</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg/220px-Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg/330px-Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg/440px-Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="951" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_summit_1945_with_Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Churchill</a>, FDR, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a> at Yalta, two months before Roosevelt's death</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By late 1943, it was apparent that the Allies would ultimately defeat the enemy, so it became increasingly important to make high-level political decisions about the course of the war and the postwar future of Europe. Roosevelt met with Churchill and the Chinese leader <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Conference" title="Cairo Conference">Cairo Conference</a> in November&#160;1943, and then went to the <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a> to confer with Churchill and Stalin. While Churchill warned of potential domination by a Stalin dictatorship over eastern Europe, Roosevelt responded with a statement summarizing his rationale for relations with Stalin: "I just have a hunch that Stalin is not that kind of a man. ... I think that if I give him everything I possibly can and ask for nothing from him in return, noblesse oblige, he won't try to annex anything and will work with me for a world of democracy and peace."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiscamble200751.E2.80.9352_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiscamble200751.E2.80.9352-259"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a>, Roosevelt and Churchill discussed plans for a postwar international organization. For his part, Stalin insisted on redrawing the frontiers of Poland. Stalin supported Roosevelt's plan for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and promised to enter the war against Japan 90 days after Germany was defeated.</p>
<p>By the beginning of 1945, however, with the Allied armies advancing into Germany and the Soviets in control of Poland, the postwar issues came into the open. In February, Roosevelt traveled to Yalta, in Crimea, to meet again with Stalin and Churchill. While Roosevelt maintained his confidence that Stalin would keep his Yalta promises regarding free elections in eastern Europe, one month after Yalta ended, Roosevelt's Ambassador to the USSR <a href="/wiki/W._Averell_Harriman" title="W. Averell Harriman">Averell Harriman</a> cabled Roosevelt that "we must come clearly to realize that the Soviet program is the establishment of totalitarianism, ending personal liberty and democracy as we know it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerthonPotts2007296.E2.80.9397_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerthonPotts2007296.E2.80.9397-260"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> Two days later, Roosevelt began to admit that his view of Stalin had been excessively optimistic and that "Averell is right."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerthonPotts2007296.E2.80.9397_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerthonPotts2007296.E2.80.9397-260"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Declining_health">Declining health</span></h3>
<p>Roosevelt, who was a chain-smoker,<sup id="cite_ref-nih_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nih-261"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smoker_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smoker-262"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> had been in declining health since at least 1940, and by 1944 he was noticeably fatigued. In March&#160;1944, shortly after his 62nd birthday, he underwent testing at <a href="/wiki/Bethesda_Naval_Hospital" title="Bethesda Naval Hospital" class="mw-redirect">Bethesda Hospital</a> and was found to have <a href="/wiki/High_blood_pressure" title="High blood pressure" class="mw-redirect">high blood pressure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atherosclerosis" title="Atherosclerosis">atherosclerosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coronary_artery_disease" title="Coronary artery disease">coronary artery disease</a> causing <a href="/wiki/Angina_pectoris" title="Angina pectoris">angina pectoris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure" title="Congestive heart failure" class="mw-redirect">congestive heart failure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970448_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970448-263"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> Hospital physicians and two outside specialists ordered Roosevelt to rest. His personal physician, Admiral Ross McIntire, created a daily schedule that banned business guests for lunch and incorporated two hours of rest each day. During the 1944 election campaign, McIntire denied several times that Roosevelt's health was poor; on October&#160;12, for example, he announced that "The President's health is perfectly OK. There are absolutely no organic difficulties at all."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther_1950372.E2.80.9374_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther_1950372.E2.80.9374-266"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to the election, Roosevelt may have used his authority over the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Censorship" title="Office of Censorship">Office of Censorship</a> to quash press reports of his declining physical health.<sup id="cite_ref-sweeney2001_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sweeney2001-267"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_1944">Election of 1944</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1944" title="United States presidential election, 1944">United States presidential election, 1944</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg/220px-RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg/330px-RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="348" data-file-height="445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RooseveltTruman1944poster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Democratic campaign poster of 1944 with Roosevelt and Truman</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roosevelt, aware that most publishers were opposed to him, issued a decree in 1943 that blocked all publishers and media executives from visits to combat areas; he put General Marshall in charge of enforcement. The main target was <a href="/wiki/Henry_Luce" title="Henry Luce">Henry Luce</a>, the powerful publisher of <i>Time</i> and <i>Life</i> magazines. Historian <a href="/wiki/Alan_Brinkley" title="Alan Brinkley">Alan Brinkley</a> argues the move was "badly mistaken", for had Luce been allowed to travel, he would have been an enthusiastic cheerleader for American forces around the globe. But stranded in New York City, Luce's frustration and anger expressed itself in hard-edged partisanship.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Party leaders insisted that Roosevelt drop <a href="/wiki/Henry_A._Wallace" title="Henry A. Wallace">Henry A. Wallace</a>, who had been erratic as Vice President and was too pro-Soviet. <a href="/wiki/James_F._Byrnes" title="James F. Byrnes">James F. Byrnes</a> of South Carolina, a top FDR aide, was considered ineligible because he had left the Catholic Church and many Catholic voters would not vote for him. Roosevelt replaced Wallace with Missouri Senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>, best known for his battle against corruption and inefficiency in wartime spending. The Republicans nominated <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey" title="Thomas E. Dewey">Thomas E. Dewey</a>, the liberal governor of New York. The opposition lambasted FDR and his administration for domestic corruption, bureaucratic inefficiency, tolerance of Communism, and military blunders. Labor unions, which had grown rapidly in the war, threw their all-out support behind Roosevelt. Roosevelt and Truman won the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1944" title="United States presidential election, 1944">1944 election</a> by a comfortable margin, defeating the Dewey and his running mate <a href="/wiki/John_W._Bricker" title="John W. Bricker">John W. Bricker</a> with 53.4% of the popular vote and 432 out of the 531 electoral votes.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The President campaigned in favor of a strong United Nations, so his victory symbolized support for the nation's future participation in the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970533_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970533-270"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the President's health and the ongoing state of war, the President's fourth inauguration on January 20, 1945, was held on the White House lawn.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970562_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970562-271"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_term_and_death.2C_1945">Fourth term and death, 1945</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_days.2C_death_and_memorial">Last days, death and memorial</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:FDR_on_quincy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FDR_on_quincy.jpg/220px-FDR_on_quincy.jpg" width="220" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FDR_on_quincy.jpg/330px-FDR_on_quincy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FDR_on_quincy.jpg/440px-FDR_on_quincy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1007" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Roosevelt meets with <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Saud_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Ibn Saud of Saudi Arabia" class="mw-redirect">King Abdul-Aziz of Saudi Arabia</a> on board the <a href="/wiki/USS_Quincy_(CA-71)" title="USS Quincy (CA-71)">USS <i>Quincy</i></a> at the <a href="/wiki/Great_Bitter_Lake" title="Great Bitter Lake">Great Bitter Lake</a> (February 14, 1945)</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:FDR-April-11-1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/FDR-April-11-1945.jpg/220px-FDR-April-11-1945.jpg" width="220" height="272" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/FDR-April-11-1945.jpg/330px-FDR-April-11-1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/FDR-April-11-1945.jpg/440px-FDR-April-11-1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2234" data-file-height="2763" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Last photograph of Roosevelt (April 11, 1945)</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg/220px-Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg" width="220" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg/330px-Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg/440px-Franklin_Roosevelt_funeral_procession_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1182" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Roosevelt's funeral procession in Washington, D.C., watched by 300,000 spectators (April 14, 1945)</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21,_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg" width="220" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg/330px-Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg/440px-Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Gravesite_August_21%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2114" data-file-height="1177" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">FDR gravesite at Hyde Park</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The President left the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> on February&#160;12, 1945, flew to Egypt and boarded the <a href="/wiki/USS_Quincy_(CA-71)" title="USS Quincy (CA-71)">USS <i>Quincy</i></a> operating on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Bitter_Lake" title="Great Bitter Lake">Great Bitter Lake</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. Aboard <i>Quincy</i>, the next day he met with <a href="/wiki/Farouk_I" title="Farouk I" class="mw-redirect">Farouk I</a>, king of Egypt, and <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie</a>, emperor of Ethiopia. On February&#160;14, he held a historic meeting with <a href="/wiki/King_Abdul_Aziz" title="King Abdul Aziz" class="mw-redirect">King Abdulaziz</a>, the founder of Saudi Arabia, a meeting some historians believe holds profound significance in U.S.-Saudi relations even today.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970578_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970578-272"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> After a final meeting between Roosevelt and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, <i>Quincy</i> steamed for Algiers, arriving February&#160;18, at which time Roosevelt conferred with American ambassadors to Britain, France and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970579_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970579-273"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> At Yalta, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wilson,_1st_Baron_Moran" title="Charles Wilson, 1st Baron Moran">Lord Moran</a>, Winston Churchill's physician, commenting on Roosevelt's ill health, said that he was a dying man.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970573_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970573-274"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When Roosevelt returned to the United States, he addressed Congress on March&#160;1 about the Yalta Conference,<sup id="cite_ref-congress45_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congress45-275"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> and many were shocked to see how old, thin and frail he looked. He spoke while seated in the well of the House, an unprecedented concession to his physical incapacity. Roosevelt opened his speech by saying, "I hope that you will pardon me for this unusual posture of sitting down during the presentation of what I want to say, but... it makes it a lot easier for me not to have to carry about ten pounds of steel around on the bottom of my legs." Still in full command mentally, he firmly stated "The Crimean Conference ought to spell the end of a system of unilateral action, the exclusive alliances, the spheres of influence, the balances of power, and all the other expedients that have been tried for centuries– and have always failed. We propose to substitute for all these, a universal organization in which all peace-loving nations will finally have a chance to join."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek1995520_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek1995520-276"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During March&#160;1945, he sent strongly worded messages to Stalin accusing him of breaking his Yalta commitments over Poland, Germany, <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> and other issues. When Stalin accused the western Allies of plotting a separate peace with Hitler behind his back, Roosevelt replied: "I cannot avoid a feeling of bitter resentment towards your informers, whoever they are, for such vile misrepresentations of my actions or those of my trusted subordinates."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970587_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970587-277"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On March&#160;29, 1945, Roosevelt went to the <a href="/wiki/Little_White_House" title="Little White House">Little White House</a> at <a href="/wiki/Warm_Springs,_Georgia" title="Warm Springs, Georgia">Warm Springs, Georgia</a>, to rest before his anticipated appearance at the founding conference of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. On the afternoon of April&#160;12, Roosevelt said, "I have a terrific pain in the back of my head." He then slumped forward in his chair, unconscious, and was carried into his bedroom. The president's attending cardiologist, Dr. Howard Bruenn, diagnosed a massive <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">cerebral hemorrhage</a> (stroke).<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> At 3:35&#160;p.m. that day, Roosevelt died. As <a href="/wiki/Allen_Drury" title="Allen Drury">Allen Drury</a> later said, "so ended an era, and so began another." After Roosevelt's death, an editorial by <i>The New York Times</i> declared, "Men will thank God on their knees a hundred years from now that Franklin D. Roosevelt was in the White House".<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the time he collapsed, Roosevelt had been sitting for a portrait painting by the artist <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Shoumatoff" title="Elizabeth Shoumatoff">Elizabeth Shoumatoff</a>, known as the famous <a href="/wiki/Unfinished_portrait_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Unfinished portrait of Franklin D. Roosevelt">Unfinished Portrait of FDR</a>.</p>
<p>In his later years at the White House, when Roosevelt was increasingly overworked, his daughter <a href="/wiki/Anna_E._Roosevelt" title="Anna E. Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect">Anna Roosevelt Boettiger</a> had moved in to provide her father companionship and support. Anna had also arranged for her father to meet with his former mistress, the now widowed <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Page_Mercer_Rutherfurd" title="Lucy Page Mercer Rutherfurd" class="mw-redirect">Lucy Mercer Rutherfurd</a>. Shoumatoff, who maintained close friendships with both Roosevelt and Mercer, rushed Mercer away to avoid negative publicity and implications of infidelity.</p>
<p>On the morning of April&#160;13, Roosevelt's body was placed in a flag-draped coffin and loaded onto the presidential train. After a White House funeral on April&#160;14, Roosevelt was transported back to Hyde Park by train. As was his wish, Roosevelt was buried in the Rose Garden of the <a href="/wiki/Home_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site" title="Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site">Springwood estate</a>, the Roosevelt family home in Hyde Park on April&#160;15. Eleanor, who died in November&#160;1962, was buried next to him.</p>
<p>Roosevelt's death was met with shock and grief<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup> across the US and around the world. His declining health had not been known to the general public.</p>
<p>Less than a month after his death, on May&#160;8, the war in Europe ended. President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a> dedicated <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">Victory in Europe Day</a> and its celebrations to Roosevelt's memory, and kept the flags across the U.S. at half-staff for the remainder of the 30-day mourning period, saying that his only wish was "that Franklin D. Roosevelt had lived to witness this day."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCullough1992345.2C_381_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCullough1992345.2C_381-281"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supreme_Court_appointments_1933.E2.80.9345">Supreme Court appointments 1933–45</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_Supreme_Court_candidates" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt Supreme Court candidates">Franklin D. Roosevelt Supreme Court candidates</a></div>
